Stop Testing Attacks, Start Diagnosing Defenses: The Four-Checkpoint Framework Reveals Where LLM Safety Breaks
Authors: Hayfa Dhabhi, Kashyap Thimmaraju
First: 2026-02-10T10:17:25+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-10T10:17:25+00:00
Comments: 17 pages, pre-print
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2
Abstract
Large Language Models (LLMs) deploy safety mechanisms to prevent harmful outputs, yet these defenses remain vulnerable to adversarial prompts. While existing research demonstrates that jailbreak attacks succeed, it does not explain \textit{where} defenses fail or \textit{why}. To address this gap, we propose that LLM safety operates as a sequential pipeline with distinct checkpoints. We introduce the \textbf{Four-Checkpoint Framework}, which organizes safety mechanisms along two dimensions: processing stage (input vs.\ output) and detection level (literal vs.\ intent). This creates four checkpoints, CP1 through CP4, each representing a defensive layer that can be independently evaluated. We design 13 evasion techniques, each targeting a specific checkpoint, enabling controlled testing of individual defensive layers. Using this framework, we evaluate GPT-5, Claude Sonnet 4, and Gemini 2.5 Pro across 3,312 single-turn, black-box test cases. We employ an LLM-as-judge approach for response classification and introduce Weighted Attack Success Rate (WASR), a severity-adjusted metric that captures partial information leakage overlooked by binary evaluation. Our evaluation reveals clear patterns. Traditional Binary ASR reports 22.6\% attack success. However, WASR reveals 52.7\%, a 2.3$\times$ higher vulnerability. Output-stage defenses (CP3, CP4) prove weakest at 72--79\% WASR, while input-literal defenses (CP1) are strongest at 13\% WASR. Claude achieves the strongest safety (42.8\% WASR), followed by GPT-5 (55.9\%) and Gemini (59.5\%). These findings suggest that current defenses are strongest at input-literal checkpoints but remain vulnerable to intent-level manipulation and output-stage techniques. The Four-Checkpoint Framework provides a structured approach for identifying and addressing safety vulnerabilities in deployed systems.
中文标题/摘要
标题：停止测试攻击，开始诊断防御：四个检查点框架揭示了大型语言模型安全性破裂的地方
大型语言模型（LLMs）部署安全机制以防止有害输出，但这些防御仍然容易受到对抗性提示的攻击。虽然现有研究表明越狱攻击成功，但并未解释防御失败的\textit{位置}或\textit{原因}。为了解决这一空白，我们提出LLM安全性作为一个具有不同检查点的顺序管道。我们引入了\textbf{四个检查点框架}，该框架沿两个维度组织安全机制：处理阶段（输入与输出）和检测级别（字面与意图）。这创建了四个检查点，CP1到CP4，每个检查点代表一个可以独立评估的防御层。我们设计了13种规避技术，每种技术针对特定检查点，从而实现对单个防御层的控制测试。使用该框架，我们对GPT-5、Claude Sonnet 4和Gemini 2.5 Pro进行了3,312个单轮黑箱测试案例的评估。我们采用LLM作为评判者的方法进行响应分类，并引入加权攻击成功率（WASR），这是一种调整严重性指标，捕捉二元评估所忽视的部分信息泄漏。我们的评估揭示了明显的模式。传统的二元ASR报告攻击成功率为22.6\%。然而，WASR显示为52.7\%，脆弱性提高了2.3$\times$。输出阶段的防御（CP3，CP4）在72--79\%的WASR中表现最弱，而输入字面防御（CP1）在13\%的WASR中表现最强。Claude的安全性最强（42.8\% WASR），其次是GPT-5（55.9\%）和Gemini（59.5\%）。这些发现表明，当前的防御在输入字面检查点最强，但仍然容易受到意图级操控和输出阶段技术的攻击。四个检查点框架为识别和解决已部署系统中的安全漏洞提供了一种结构化的方法。
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the vulnerabilities of safety mechanisms in Large Language Models (LLMs) against adversarial prompts, highlighting a gap in understanding where and why these defenses fail. Previous methods primarily focused on demonstrating the success of jailbreak attacks without a systematic analysis of defense failures. The proposed Four-Checkpoint Framework organizes safety mechanisms into four distinct checkpoints based on processing stage and detection level, allowing for targeted evaluation of individual defensive layers. This framework is well-motivated as it provides a structured approach to diagnose safety vulnerabilities. The methodology includes designing 13 evasion techniques and evaluating models like GPT-5, Claude Sonnet 4, and Gemini 2.5 Pro across 3,312 test cases using a novel metric called Weighted Attack Success Rate (WASR). The findings indicate that traditional binary evaluations underestimate vulnerabilities, revealing a 52.7% attack success rate with WASR compared to 22.6% with binary metrics, thus supporting the need for improved diagnostic frameworks in LLM safety.
本研究关注大型语言模型（LLMs）安全机制在面对对抗性提示时的脆弱性，指出现有研究虽然展示了越狱攻击的成功，但未能明确这些防御的具体失败点。以往的方法主要集中在攻击成功率的二元评估上，这不足以充分捕捉防御脆弱性的细微差别。提出的四检查点框架将安全机制组织成一个顺序管道，设有四个不同的检查点，从而允许对每个防御层进行更详细的评估。该框架的提出具有良好的动机，因为它能够识别出以前被忽视的LLM防御中的弱点。该方法论涉及设计13种规避技术来测试这些检查点，并在3,312个测试案例中评估GPT-5、Claude Sonnet 4和Gemini 2.5 Pro等模型。研究结果表明，传统的二元指标低估了脆弱性，揭示了加权攻击成功率（WASR）为52.7%，显著高于22.6%的二元成功率，从而表明当前防御在输出阶段检查点特别薄弱。
CAGE: A Framework for Culturally Adaptive Red-Teaming Benchmark Generation
Authors: Chaeyun Kim, YongTaek Lim, Kihyun Kim, Junghwan Kim, Minwoo Kim
Venue: ICLR 2026
First: 2026-02-09T22:01:32+00:00 · Latest: 2026-02-09T22:01:32+00:00
Comments: Accepted at ICLR 2026
Abs · PDF · Code1 · Code2 · Code3
Abstract
Existing red-teaming benchmarks, when adapted to new languages via direct translation, fail to capture socio-technical vulnerabilities rooted in local culture and law, creating a critical blind spot in LLM safety evaluation. To address this gap, we introduce CAGE (Culturally Adaptive Generation), a framework that systematically adapts the adversarial intent of proven red-teaming prompts to new cultural contexts. At the core of CAGE is the Semantic Mold, a novel approach that disentangles a prompt's adversarial structure from its cultural content. This approach enables the modeling of realistic, localized threats rather than testing for simple jailbreaks. As a representative example, we demonstrate our framework by creating KoRSET, a Korean benchmark, which proves more effective at revealing vulnerabilities than direct translation baselines. CAGE offers a scalable solution for developing meaningful, context-aware safety benchmarks across diverse cultures. Our dataset and evaluation rubrics are publicly available at https://github.com/selectstar-ai/CAGE-paper. (WARNING: This paper contains model outputs that can be offensive in nature.)
中文标题/摘要
标题：CAGE：一种文化适应性红队基准生成框架
现有的红队基准在通过直接翻译适应新语言时，未能捕捉到根植于当地文化和法律的社会技术漏洞，造成了LLM安全评估中的一个关键盲点。为了解决这一问题，我们引入了CAGE（文化适应性生成），这是一个系统性地将经过验证的红队提示的对抗意图适应新文化背景的框架。CAGE的核心是语义模具，这是一种新颖的方法，将提示的对抗结构与其文化内容分离。这种方法使得能够建模现实的、本地化的威胁，而不是仅仅测试简单的越狱。作为一个代表性例子，我们通过创建KoRSET，一个韩国基准，展示了我们的框架，该基准在揭示漏洞方面比直接翻译基线更有效。CAGE为在多元文化中开发有意义的、上下文感知的安全基准提供了可扩展的解决方案。我们的数据集和评估标准可在https://github.com/selectstar-ai/CAGE-paper上公开获取。（警告：本文包含可能具有冒犯性的模型输出。）
Summary / 总结
The research addresses the limitations of existing red-teaming benchmarks that, when translated into new languages, overlook socio-technical vulnerabilities tied to local culture and legal contexts, which poses a significant risk in evaluating the safety of large language models (LLMs). Previous methods primarily relied on direct translation, which failed to capture the nuanced adversarial intent relevant to different cultures, leading to ineffective assessments. The proposed CAGE framework introduces a Semantic Mold that separates a prompt's adversarial structure from its cultural content, allowing for the generation of culturally relevant threats rather than simplistic tests. This approach is well-motivated as it aims to enhance the safety evaluation process across diverse cultural contexts. The paper contributes by presenting CAGE and demonstrating its application through the creation of KoRSET, a Korean benchmark that outperforms direct translation methods in identifying vulnerabilities, thus supporting the goal of developing context-aware safety benchmarks for LLMs. The methodology involves systematically adapting red-teaming prompts to local cultural contexts, resulting in more effective evaluations of LLM safety.
本研究解决了现有红队基准的局限性，这些基准在通过直接翻译适应新语言时，往往无法考虑特定于当地文化和法律的社会技术漏洞。以往的方法未能充分捕捉这些细微差别，导致在评估大型语言模型（LLMs）安全性时出现关键盲点。提出的CAGE框架引入了一种语义模具，能够将提示的对抗结构与其文化内容分离，从而生成本地化威胁，而不仅仅是测试基本漏洞。该方法的动机明确，旨在增强跨文化背景的安全评估的相关性和有效性。本文贡献了一种创建文化适应性基准的新方法，示例是为韩语开发的KoRSET基准，该基准在揭示漏洞方面表现出比传统翻译方法更高的有效性，从而支持改善LLM安全评估的目标。
